< text>
Brownies.
From an old Irish bar to a budding spacious alcove in the pocket area of Sacramento.
The bar still retains, as of 8/28/19, the name Brownies. Some of the old patrons still frequent during day hours, and sometimes into the night. The climate of the new blends with the changing winds of the new ownership, but the mood and effect still welcomes the intimate experience of your favorite hole-in-the-wall bar.
You can get some fantastic Mexican from a wonderful restaurant nearby, right at the bar. The magic in the experience comes from the people that still continue to frequent the new direction.
The new design has booth seating and pool tables with sports channels available, but I think you'll come for the experience.
Cash only, but there's an ATM inside.
These kinds of places are what I seek in the town I love.< /text>

<review>I miss Brownie's. The old Brownie's that is, not this place. Although the address is the same, this neighborhood bar has been scrubbed, remodeled and robbed of its soul. The new ambiance tries too hard to be midtown modern and chic. In such a stylized plaza, a half mile from Eichler street, they have missed the rehab mark of this landmark by a mile. Such a wasted opportunity. Loud, tacky and unimaginative is their aesthetic. We walked in for an after dinner cocktail and walked out before we reached the bar. We will not be back. Such a shame and a loss for this mid-mod neighborhood.</review>< Pictures>

My friend and I had one beer when he went to purchase another beer the bar tender took his $50 bill and then turned to him saying its fake and wouldn't give it back. And had the bouncer remove us from the bar, I have never been so embarrassed in my life. They didn't even check the bill with a marker, they just took it and sed it was fake and refused to give it back. But lucky for us we new a few other guys that were there and they helped us get the $50 bill back. We went to the liquor store right next to Brownies and the man checked the $50 bill for us. I bounce around to different shops for my annual AAA free diagnostic printout. People scoff, but this practice has saved me from dishonest recommendations, and reinforced the honest ones. 1567488675142< /time>
<userid>106689967933838920220<//userid><user_name>Srikumar Chari</user_name>< Text>
Nice Indian restaurant with a twist. We went after it was mentioned in the Check please (KQED) program. The offer a couple traditional Indian appetizers, like Samosa. The entrees have both a Mexican twist, i.e., chicken enchiladas but the spicing is all Indian. The Italian style entrees are Indian entrees served on a bed of zucchini spaghetti, etc. But the kicker is actually different, the chef/owner of the place asks if he can bring entrees of his choice. Three vegetarians on the table went with that option - they were quite happy with the selection. I went with the chicken enchiladas, very good interesting flavors - Indian, plus traditional Mexican flavors and the side rice is Indian style. The owner makes a fun game out of the chef's choice entrees - he asks you to guess what the vegetables are, if you get all of them right the entire meal is free! I don't know if anyone got all right, we gave up about 30% of the way.

The place is a bit small, so cozy is the word. It can get crowded. Note in Google maps directions - it asks you to take that last right and claims.you've arrived... Not really you have to turn into the strip and the 3rd place is Avatar's.

Bottom line, worth a visit.<//Text>

Amazing twist to conventional Indian cuisine. I like going here after every 5-6 months (mainly because it is a bit far from South Bay) to revisit this innovative way of mixing up Indian dishes. The best thing is that there is no compromise to the taste at all. The dishes are well thought of and the final outcome is delicious. Enchiladas were best. If having an amazing meal in a quick time is your metric, you‚Äôre going to love it here. The owner is enthusiastic and provides lots of inputs, but can hurry you into ordering at times. The ambience is just alright for a joint in the upscale neighborhood of Sausalito, can certainly go through an uplift.<//Review>

112306781013376612499</user_id>
< user_name>
Biren Parmar</user_name>
<time>1532978681858< /time>< Rate>
5</Rate>
< Text>
This review focuses on the vegetarian dishes we had at Avatar's. Imagine being able to order flavorful dishes made from ingredients used in traditional Indian cooking, an alien concept in a vast majority of Indian restaurants in the US. I personally don't have a problem with the Indian restaurant experience, but after a while, it starts to get repetitive - it's the same set of dishes on the menu everywhere (at least this seems to be the case for the vegetarian section of the menu). The guys at Avatar's excel at using not-so-commonly used veggies and greens in their preparations. Then, they take it up a notch and make fusion dishes out of these ingredients, which is simply mind blowing. The entire experience of the visit was awesome, not very different from some of the other reviewers here. Definitely going back.
An afterthought: We had been a little skeptical about going to the place after an underwhelming experience at one of the other branches of Avatar's in the area months ago. But the amount of positive feedback we got about the place, especially even from non-Indians, made the itch to pay a visit at least once irresistible. This is a completely different and unique experience.</Text>

<Date>1459911246828<//Date>< review>
When researching places to eat near the Golden Gate, my fiance came upon Avatar's.  We, both, love Indian food and the previous reviews piqued our interest.  When we arrived, Avatar greeted us and promised a culinary adventure.  After ascertaining our food likes/dislikes, and my fiance's dietary needs, he delivered the best meal we had since arriving.  My fiance loved his personal story.  We have nothing like this in Kentucky and are definitely missing out on something wonderful.  We will return to San Francisco, and to Avatar's, without a doubt.</review>

Avatar is a small magical restaurant that infuses quality, natural and healing spices in all of their foods. There is no dairy, sugar or gluten in this restaurant. <Review>This is by far the best Indian restaurant in the Bay Area. I make this bold statement as an Indian person with a talented cook for a mother and countless experiences eating at Indian restaurants while growing up in the area. This restaurant best exemplifies healthy, tasteful Indian cuisine, as well as some incredible fusion dishes (I had to go back several times to try all the Punjabi enchiladas). The masala chai is always freshly made to order, and you can be confident that anything you order is made with the best ingredients.

By food quality alone this place deserves 5 stars. The owner, a delightful man who greets every customer and takes every order, will make your experience personalized and extraordinary. Aside from his deep knowledge as a nutritionist, he is deeply engaged in the customer experience and is a perfect example of how to run a successful business for decades. Just as his food exemplifies healthy and tasteful food of India, his personality exemplifies the work ethic and dharmic sense of responsibility of India.

This is truly one of the hidden gems of California and I whole-heartedly recommend this restaurant to everyone.< /Review><Gmap_id>0x808585050d11d18d:0xe1d770086a096be</Gmap_id><Rating>5< /Rating><user>112963650635319312928< /user>< Pics>
